When in doubt, refer to the Google guide first, then apply these project-specific patterns.\n   173→\n   174→Key areas from the Google guide to pay special attention to:\n   175→\n   176→- **Formatting**: Use `gofmt` (we use `goimports` which includes `gofmt`)\n   177→- **Naming**: Follow Go naming conventions for packages, types, functions, and variables\n   178→- **Package organization**: Keep packages focused and avoid circular dependencies\n   179→- **Error handling**: Return errors as the last return value, handle errors explicitly\n   180→- **Documentation**: Write clear godoc comments for exported types and functions\n   181→\n   182→#### Naming Conventions\n   183→\n   184→- **Public functions**: Use PascalCase (`NewServer`, `ListFlags`, `RegisterGRPC`)\n   185→- **Private functions**: Use camelCase (`getStore`, `buildConfig`, `handleError`)\n   186→- **Factory functions**: Use `New` prefix for constructors (`NewRepository`, `NewEnvironmentFactory`)\n   187→- **Variables**: Use camelCase (`environmentKey`, `namespaceKey`, `startTime`)\n   188→- **Constants**: Use PascalCase for exported, camelCase for unexported\n   189→- **Interfaces**: Use descriptive names (`Store`, `EnvironmentStore`, `Validator`)\n   190→\n   191→#### Variable Declarations\n   192→\n   193→```go\n   194→// Prefer := for single variable declarations\n   195→result := SomeType{}\n   196→\n   197→// Use var blocks for multiple related variables\n   198→var (\n   199→    environmentKey = r.EnvironmentKey\n   200→    namespaceKey   = r.NamespaceKey\n   201→    startTime      = time.Now().UTC()\n   202→)\n   203→```\n   204→\n   205→#### Constants\n   206→\n   207→Use constants when appropriate for values that are unlikely to change. Even in tests.\n   208→\n   209→**❌ Bad Examples**\n   210→\n   211→```go\n   212→var (\n   213→    maxRetries = 3\n   214→    secretProvider = \"vault\"\n   215→)\n   216→```\n   217→\n   218→```go\n secretProvider = \"vault\"\n   229→)\n   230→```\n   231→\n   232→#### Error Handling\n   233→\n   234→##### Error Types\n   235→\n   236→Use the custom error types when possible:\n   237→\n   238→```go\n   239→// Preferred - use custom error types\n   240→return nil, errs.ErrNotFoundf(\"flag %q not found\", key)\n   241→return nil, errs.ErrInvalidf(\"invalid configuration: %s\", reason)\n   242→\n   243→// Fallback - standard error handling\n   244→return nil, fmt.Errorf(\"failed to process: %w\", err)\n   245→```\n   246→\n   247→##### Inline Errors\n   248→\n   249→Prefer inline error declarations and checking when it makes sense.\n   250→\n   251→**❌ Bad Example**\n   252→\n   253→```go\n   254→err := doSomething()\n   255→if err != nil {\n   256→    // ...\n   257→}\n   258→```\n 278→\n   279→    // Third-party packages\n   280→    \"github.com/go-git/go-git/v6\"\n   281→    \"go.uber.org/zap\"\n   282→\n   283→    // Local packages\n   284→    \"go.flipt.io/flipt/errors\"\n   285→    \"go.flipt.io/flipt/internal/config\"\n   286→)\n   287→```\n   288→\n   289→#### Logging\n   290→\n   291→Use structured logging with zap:\n   292→\n   293→```go\n   294→// Preferred - structured logging with context\n   295→s.logger.Debug(\"processing request\", \n   296→    zap.String(\"environment\", envKey),\n   297→    zap.String(\"namespace\", nsKey),\n   298→    zap.Int(\"count\", len(items)))\n   299→\n   300→// Use appropriate log levels\n   301→s.logger.Debug(\"debug info for development\")  // Most common\n   302→s.logger.Info(\"important application events\")\n   303→s.logger.Warn(\"recoverable error conditions\")\n   304→s.logger.Error(\"error conditions that need attention\")\n   305→\n   306→// Avoid overusing log statements - be selective about what to log\n   307→```\n   308→\n   309→#### Comments and Documentation\n   310→\n   311→```go\n   312→// Public functions need godoc comments starting with function name\n   313→// ListFlags common.FliptEnvironmentFromContext(ctx); ok && headerEnv != \"\" {\n   319→        environmentKey = headerEnv\n   320→    }\n   321→}\n   322→```\n   323→\n   324→#### Project Organization\n   325→\n Playwright for E2E\n   410→\n   411→### Writing Effective Tests\n   412→\n   413→When writing tests, ensure they actually verify the functionality being tested:\n   414→\n   415→**❌ Bad Example - Test doesn't verify actual behavior:**\n   416→\n   417→```go\n   418→// This test only verifies the method runs without error, not that the logic works\n   419→func TestFeature(t *testing.T) {\n   420→    result, err := service.DoSomething(input)\n   421→    require.NoError(t, err)\n   422→    assert.NotNil(t, result)\n   423→}\n   424→```\n   425→\n   426→**✅ Good Example - Test verifies specific behavior:**\n   427→\n   428→```go\n   429→// This test verifies the actual logic and behavior\n   430→func TestFeature(t *testing.T) {\n   431→    // Use mock.MatchedBy to verify the correct data is passed through\n   432→    store.On(\"Method\", mock.MatchedBy(func(ctx context.Context) bool {\n   433→        // Verify the context contains the expected values\n   434→        value, ok := somePackage.ValueFromContext(ctx)\n   435→        return ok && value == expectedValue\n   436→    }), expectedArg).Return(expectedResult, nil)\n   437→    \n   438→    result, err := service.DoSomething(input)\n   439→    require.NoError(t, err)\n   440→    \n   441→    // Verify the actual business logic worked correctly\n   442→    assert.Equal(t, expectedOutput, result.ImportantField)\n   443→    store.AssertExpectations(t) // Ensures mocks were called as expected\n   444→}\n   445→```\n   446→\n   447→**Key Testing Principles:**\n   448→\n   449→- **Verify behavior, not just success**: Don't just check that methods return without error\n   450→- **Test the logic**: Use `mock.MatchedBy` to verify correct data flows through the system\n   451→- **Test edge cases**: Include tests for when conditions are met vs. not met\n   452→- **Use meaningful assertions**: Assert on the specific values that matter to the business logic\n   453→- **Mock verification**: Use `mock.AssertExpectations(t)` to ensure mocks were called with expected parameters\n   454→\n   455→### Integration Tests\n   456→\n   457→Integration tests are defined in `build/testing/` and run as Mage targets. evaluation cache\"\n   509→\n   510→git commit -s -m \"test: improve X-Environment header test coverage\n   511→\n   512→- Use mock.MatchedBy to verify context contains correct environment\n   513→- Add test for when header is not present\n   514→- Ensure tests actually validate the header precedence logic\"\n   515→```\n   516→\n   517→### Pull Request Guidelines\n   518→\n   519→#### PR Title When in doubt, refer to the Google guide first, then apply these project-specific patterns.\n\nKey areas from the Google guide to pay special attention to:\n\n- **Formatting**: Use `gofmt` (we use `goimports` which includes `gofmt`)\n- **Naming**: Follow Go naming conventions for packages, types, functions, and variables\n- **Package organization**: Keep packages focused and avoid circular dependencies\n- **Error handling**: Return errors as the last return value, handle errors explicitly\n- **Documentation**: Write clear godoc comments for exported types and functions\n\n#### Naming Conventions\n\n- **Public functions**: Use PascalCase (`NewServer`, `ListFlags`, `RegisterGRPC`)\n- **Private functions**: Use camelCase (`getStore`, `buildConfig`, `handleError`)\n- **Factory functions**: Use `New` prefix for constructors (`NewRepository`, `NewEnvironmentFactory`)\n- **Variables**: Use camelCase (`environmentKey`, `namespaceKey`, `startTime`)\n- **Constants**: Use PascalCase for exported, camelCase for unexported\n- **Interfaces**: Use descriptive names (`Store`, `EnvironmentStore`, `Validator`)\n\n#### Variable Declarations\n\n```go\n// Prefer := for single variable declarations\nresult := SomeType{}\n\n// Use var blocks for multiple related variables\nvar (\n    environmentKey = r.EnvironmentKey\n    namespaceKey   = r.NamespaceKey\n    startTime      = time.Now().UTC()\n)\n```\n\n#### Constants\n\nUse constants when appropriate for values that are unlikely to change. Even in tests.\n\n**❌ Bad Examples**\n\n```go\nvar (\n    maxRetries = 3\n    secretProvider = \"vault\"\n)\n```\n\n```go\n  maxRetries := 3\n  secretProvider := \"vault\"\n```\n\n**✅ Good Example**\n\n```go\nconst (\n    maxRetries = 3\n    secretProvider = \"vault\"\n)\n```\n\n#### Error Handling\n\n##### Error Types\n\nUse the custom error types when possible:\n\n```go\n// Preferred - use custom error types\nreturn nil, errs.ErrNotFoundf(\"flag %q not found\", key)\nreturn nil, errs.ErrInvalidf(\"invalid configuration: %s\", reason)\n\n// Fallback - standard error handling\nreturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"failed to process: %w\", err)\n```\n\n##### Inline Errors\n\nPrefer inline error declarations and checking when it makes sense.\n\n**❌ Bad Example**\n\n```go\nerr := doSomething()\nif err != nil {\n    // ...\n}\n```\n\n**✅ Good Example**\n\n```go\nif err := doSomething(); err != nil {\n    // ...\n}\n```\n\n#### Imports\n\nFollow the three-group import pattern (extends Google guide):\n\n```go\nimport (\n    // Standard library\n    \"context\"\n    \"fmt\"\n    \"time\"\n\n    // Third-party packages\n    \"github.com/go-git/go-git/v6\"\n    \"go.uber.org/zap\"\n\n    // Local packages\n    \"go.flipt.io/flipt/errors\"\n    \"go.flipt.io/flipt/internal/config\"\n)\n```\n\n#### Logging\n\nUse structured logging with zap:\n\n```go\n// conditions\")\ns.logger.Error(\"error conditions that need attention\")\n\n// Avoid overusing log statements - be selective about what to log\n```\n\n#### Comments and Documentation\n\n```go\n// Public functions need godoc comments starting with function name\n// ListFlags lists all flags in the specified environment and namespace\nfunc (s *Server) ListFlags(ctx context.Context, r *flipt.ListFlagRequest) (*flipt.FlagList, error) {\n    // Inline comments explain complex logic\n    // Check for X-Environment header for backward compatibility\n    environmentKey := r.EnvironmentKey\n    if headerEnv, ok := common.FliptEnvironmentFromContext(ctx); ok && headerEnv != \"\" {\n        environmentKey = headerEnv\n    }\n}\n```\n\n#### Project Organization\n\n- Use `internal/` for private packages that shouldn't be imported externally\n- Organize by domain (`server/`, `storage/`, `config/`, `analytics/`)\n- Keep interfaces in domain root, implementations in subdirectories\n- Co-locate tests with implementation (`*_test.go`)\n- Use `testdata/` directories for test fixtures\n\n#### Pre-commit Quality Checks (Go)\n\n**Always run these commands when adding or editing Go code:**\n\n```bash\n# Format Go code\nmage go:fmt\n\n# Lint Go code\nmage go:lint\n\n# Run modernize to update code to 1.24+ style\nmage go:modernize\n```\n\n### UI/React/TypeScript Code Style\n\n#### File Naming and Organization\n\n- **Components**: Use PascalCase for `.tsx` files (`FlagForm.tsx`, `FlagTable.tsx`)\n- **API files**: Use camelCase with suffix (`flagsApi.ts`, `authApi.ts`)\n- **Types**: Use PascalCase for `.ts` files (`Flag.ts`, `Analytics.ts`)\n- **Utilities**: Use descriptive lowercase names (`helpers.ts`)\n\n#### Component Structure\n\n- Use functional components with hooks\n- Organize components by domain in directories\n- Keep reusable UI components in `ui/` directory\n- Co-locate component tests with implementation\n\n#### State Management\n\n- Use Redux Toolkit for application state\n- Create API slices for domain-specific data (`flagsApi.ts`)\n- Use TypeScript for type safety throughout\n\n#### Pre-commit Quality Checks (UI)\n\n**Always run these commands when adding or editing UI code:**\n\n```bash\n# Format UI code (TypeScript/React)\nmage ui:fmt\n\n# Lint UI code (ESLint)\nmage ui:lint\n```\n\n### General Pre-commit Checks\n\n```bash\n# Format specific markdown files (replace with actual filename)\nnpx prettier -w README.md\n```\n\n## Configuration\n\n### Configuration Files\n\n- `config/local.yml` - Local development config\n- `config/dev.yml` - Alternative dev config\n- User config at `{{ USER_CONFIG_DIR }}/flipt/config.yml`\n\n### Debugging Tips\n\n- Use `FLIPT_LOG_LEVEL=debug` for verbose logging\n- Check `/metrics` endpoint for Prometheus metrics\n- View OpenTelemetry traces for request flow\n- Git sync issues: Check repository access and credentials\n- Authentication issues: Verify redirect URLs and client configurations\n\n## Testing Guidelines\n\n### Test Structure\n\n- Go tests use testcontainers for unit tests that depend on external tools\n- UI tests use Jest for unit tests and Playwright for E2E\n\n### Writing Effective Tests\n\nWhen writing tests, ensure they actually verify the functionality being tested:\n\n**❌ Bad Example - Test doesn't verify actual behavior:**\n\n```go\n// This test only verifies the method runs without error, not that the logic works\nfunc TestFeature(t *testing.T) {\n    result, err := service.DoSomething(input)\n    require.NoError(t, err)\n    assert.NotNil(t, result)\n}\n```\n\n**✅ Good Example - Test verifies specific behavior:**\n\n```go\n// This test verifies the actual logic and behavior\nfunc TestFeature(t *testing.T) {\n    // Use mock.MatchedBy to verify the correct data is passed through\n    store.On(\"Method\", mock.MatchedBy(func(ctx context.Context) bool {\n        // Verify the context contains the expected values\n        value, ok := somePackage.ValueFromContext(ctx)\n        return ok && value == expectedValue\n    }), expectedArg).Return(expectedResult, nil)\n    \n    result, err := service.DoSomething(input)\n    require.NoError(t, err)\n    \n    // Verify the actual business logic worked correctly\n    assert.Equal(t, expectedOutput, result.ImportantField)\n    store.AssertExpectations(t) // Ensures mocks were called as expected\n}\n```\n\n**Key Testing Principles:**\n\n- **Verify behavior, not just success**: Don't just check that methods return without error\n- **Test the logic**: Use `mock.MatchedBy` to verify correct data flows through the system\n- **Test edge cases**: Include tests for when conditions are met vs. not met\n- **Use meaningful assertions**: Assert on the specific values that matter to the business logic\n- **Mock verification**: Use `mock.AssertExpectations(t)` to ensure mocks were called with expected parameters\n\n### Integration Tests\n\nIntegration tests are defined in `build/testing/` and run as Mage targets. For details on available integration test targets, helpers, and how to add new integration tests, see the files in that directory:\n\n- `build/testing/integration.go` - Integration test Mage targets and configuration\n- `build/testing/integration/` - Individual integration test suites\n- `build/testing/helpers.go` - Shared test helpers\n- `build/testing/test.go` - Core test utilities\n\n## Git Workflow & Commits\n\n### Creating Effective Commits\n\n#### Commit Message Format\n\nFollow conventional commit format:\n\n```\ntype(scope): brief description\n\nLonger description if needed explaining the why, not the what.\n\n- List specific changes if helpful\n- Include any breaking changes\n- Reference issues (e.g., \"Fixes #123\")\n```\n\n#### Commit Types\n\n- `feat:` - New features\n- `fix:` - Bug fixes\n- `docs:` - Documentation changes\n- `style:` - Code style changes (formatting, etc.)\n- `refactor:` - Code refactoring without functional changes\n- `test:` - Adding or modifying tests\n- `chore:` - Build process or auxiliary tool changes\n\n#### Examples\n\n```bash\n# Good commit messages\ngit commit -s -m \"feat: add X-Environment header support to ListFlags endpoint\n\nThe v1 ListFlags endpoint now checks for X-Environment header \nfor backward compatibility. When present, the header value \ntakes precedence over the request environment parameter.\n\n- Modified ListFlags method to check context for environment header\n- Added ForwardFliptEnvironment middleware to v1 API gateway\n- Added comprehensive test coverage\n\nFixes #4411\"\n\ngit commit -s -m \"fix: resolve race condition in flag evaluation cache\"\n\ngit commit -s -m \"test: improve X-Environment header test coverage\n\n- Use mock.MatchedBy to verify context contains correct environment\n- Add test for when header is not present\n- Ensure tests actually validate the header precedence logic\"\n```\n\n### Pull Request Guidelines\n\n#### PR Title Format\n\nUse the same conventional commit format for PR titles:\n\n```\ntype(scope): brief description\n```\n\n#### PR Description Template\n\n```markdown\n## Summary\n\nBrief description of what this PR does and why.\n\n## Changes\n\n- **Modified `file1.go`**: Specific change description\n- **Added `file2_test.go`**: Test coverage description\n- **Updated `config.yml`**: Configuration change description\n\n## Backward Compatibility\n\nDescribe any backward compatibility or breaking change considerations.\n\n## Additional Notes\n\nAny other context, screenshots, or related issues.\n```\n\n#### PR Best Practices\n\n- **Keep PRs focused**: One logical change per PR\n- **Write descriptive titles**: Use conventional commit format\n- **Provide context**: Explain the \"why\" behind changes\n- **Include tests**: Always add tests for new functionality\n- **Run quality checks**: Format and lint before creating PR\n- **Reference issues**: Use \"Fixes #123\" to auto-close issues\n- **Review your own PR**: Look through the diff before requesting review\n- **Base PRs on the correct branch**: Base PRs on the correct branch (e.g. `v2` for v2 changes, `main` for v1 changes)\n- **Label PRs correctly**: When creating a feature based off of the v2 branch, label the PR with the `v2` label. Similarly for a v1 (main) feature, use the `v1` label.\n\n#### Quality Checklist\n\nBefore creating a PR, ensure:\n\n- [ ] Code follows style guidelines\n- [ ] Tests are added and passing\n- [ ] Linting passes (`mage go:lint` / `mage ui:lint`)\n- [ ] Code is formatted (`mage go:fmt` / `mage ui:fmt`)\n- [ ] Commit messages are clear and descriptive\n- [ ] PR description explains the change and its purpose\n","numLines":571,"startLine":1,"totalLines":571}}}

493→\t\tder := x509.MarshalPKCS1PrivateKey(privateKey)\n   494→\t\tblock := &pem.Block{\n   495→\t\t\tType:  \"RSA PRIVATE KEY\",\n   496→\t\t\tBytes: der,\n   497→\t\t}\n   498→\t\tvar buf Architecture\n    75→\n    76→The integration testing system uses a sophisticated container orchestration approach:\n    77→\n    78→1. **Base Container**: Contains Go toolchain and test binaries\n    79→2. **Flipt Container**: Runs Flipt server with various configurations\n    80→3. **Service Containers**: External dependencies (Gitea, Vault, OIDC providers)\n    81→4. **Test Execution**: Runs in Dagger CLI\n   106→brew install dagger/tap/dagger\n   107→\n   108→# Run all tests (parallel execution)\n   109→dagger call test --source=. integration\n   110→\n   111→# Run specific authentication 131→\n   132→**Cache Strategy:**\n   133→- **Cache Backend**: GitHub Container Registry (GHCR) - `ghcr.io/owner/repo-cache`\n   134→- **Cache Key Format**: `flipt-{git-commit}-{source-hash}`\n   135→- uses a multi-layered build system combining:\n\n- **Mage**: Build automation tool for Go projects (like Make but in Go)\n- **Dagger**: Container-based CI/CD engine for reproducible builds\n- **npm**: UI build system for React frontend\n- **GitHub Actions**: CI/CD workflows\n\n## Directory Structure\n\n```\nbuild/\n├── README.md                 # Dagger build documentation\n├── main.go                   # Dagger module entry point\n├── dagger.gen.go            # Dagger generated code\n├── internal/                # Build system internals\n│   ├── dagger/              # Dagger client code\n│   ├── flipt.go            # Main Flipt build functions\n│   ├── ui.go               # UI build functions\n│   └── cmd/                # Build utilities\n│       ├── discover/       # OIDC test server       ├── authz/         # Authorization tests\n        ├── environments/  # Environment API tests\n        ├── ofrep/         # OpenFeature tests\n        ├── signing/       # Git signing tests\n        └── snapshot/      # Snapshot API tests\n```\n\n## Build Commands\n\n### Dagger Commands (Container-based)\n\n#### Build Commands\n\n```bash\ndagger call build                    # Build production approach:\n\n1. **Base Container**: Contains Go toolchain and test binaries\n2. **Flipt Container**: Runs Flipt server with various configurations\n3. **Service Containers**: External dependencies (Gitea, Vault, OIDC providers)\n4. **Test Execution**: Runs in isolated containers with service bindings\n\n### Available Test Cases\n\nTest cases are defined in `build/testing/integration.go:AllCases`:\n\n### Test Infrastructure\n\n#### Service Dependencies\n\n- **Gitea**: Git repository hosting for storage backends\n- **Vault**: HashiCorp Vault for secret management\n- **OIDC Provider**: Custom OIDC server for Kubernetes auth testing\n\n#### Test Data\n\n- `build/testing/integration/testdata/`: Test configuration files\n- `build/testing/integration/*/`: Individual test suite implementations\n\n### Running Integration Tests\n\n#### Local Development\n\n```bash\n# Install Dagger CLI\nbrew install dagger/tap/dagger\n\n# Run all tests (parallel execution)\ndagger call test --source=. integration\n\n# Run specific authentication tests\ndagger call test --source=. integration --cases=\"authn/token authn/jwt\"\n\n# Run with coverage collection\ndagger call test-coverage --source=. integration-coverage --cases=\"snapshot\" export --path=/tmp/coverage.out\n```\n\n#### CI/CD Pipeline\n\nGitHub Actions workflow (`.github/workflows/integration-test.yml`):\n\n1. **Test Discovery**: Extract test cases from `integration.go`\n2. **Cache Build**: Build Flipt once and push to GHCR for sharing across jobs\n3. **Matrix Execution**: Run each test case in parallel using cached images\n4. **Coverage Collection**: Aggregate coverage from all test runs\n5. **Codecov Upload**: Submit coverage reports\n\n#### Registry Cache Optimization\n\nThe CI pipeline uses Docker BuildKit registry cache to share container images across GitHub Actions jobs:\n\n**Cache Strategy:**\n- **Cache Backend**: GitHub Container Registry (GHCR) - `ghcr.io/owner/repo-cache`\n- **Cache Key Format**: `flipt-{git-commit}-{source-hash}`\n- **Cache Scope**: Per repository, shared across all PR and push workflows\n\n**Performance Benefits:**\n- **Before**: Each integration test job rebuilds Flipt (~5-10 minutes each)\n- **After**: One build job (~10 minutes) + fast test jobs using cache (~2-3 minutes each)\n- **Total reduction**: ~60% in pipeline execution time\n- **Resource savings**: Significant reduction in GitHub Actions minutes\n\n**Cache Workflow:**\n```yaml\nbuild-cache:\n  - Generate cache key from git commit + source file hashes\n  - Check if cached image exists in GHCR\n  - Build and push only if cache miss\n  - Output image reference for test jobs\n\nintegration-tests:\n  - Pull cached image from GHCR\n  - Run tests using pre-built Flipt container\n  - Maintain full test isolation and coverage\n```\n\n**Cache Management:**\n- **Invalidation**: Automatic via content-based cache keys\n- **Cleanup**: Images cleaned up after successful pipeline runs\n- **Fallback**: Graceful fallback to fresh builds if cache fails\n- **Authentication**: Uses `GITHUB_TOKEN` with `packages: write` permission\n\n### Test Configuration Patterns\n\n#### Authentication Setup\n\nTests configure Flipt with various auth methods:\n\n```go\n// Token authentication\nflipt = flipt.\n    WithEnvVariable(\"FLIPT_AUTHENTICATION_REQUIRED\", \"true\").\n    WithEnvVariable(\"FLIPT_AUTHENTICATION_METHODS_TOKEN_ENABLED\", \"true\").\n    WithEnvVariable(\"FLIPT_AUTHENTICATION_METHODS_TOKEN_STORAGE_TOKENS_BOOTSTRAP_CREDENTIAL\", \"s3cr3t\")\n\n// JWT authentication  \nflipt = flipt.\n    WithEnvVariable(\"FLIPT_AUTHENTICATION_METHODS_JWT_ENABLED\", \"true\").\n    WithEnvVariable(\"FLIPT_AUTHENTICATION_METHODS_JWT_PUBLIC_KEY_FILE\", \"/etc/flipt/jwt.pem\")\n```\n\n#### Storage Configuration\n\n```go\n// Git-based storage\nflipt = flipt.\n    WithEnvVariable(\"FLIPT_STORAGE_DEFAULT_REMOTE\", \"http://gitea:3000/root/features.git\").\n    WithEnvVariable(\"FLIPT_STORAGE_DEFAULT_BRANCH\", \"main\").\n    WithEnvVariable(\"FLIPT_CREDENTIALS_DEFAULT_TYPE\", \"basic\")\n```\n\n#### Secrets Management\n\n```go\n// File-based secrets\nflipt = flipt.\n    WithEnvVariable(\"FLIPT_SECRETS_PROVIDERS_FILE_ENABLED\", \"true\").\n    WithEnvVariable(\"FLIPT_SECRETS_PROVIDERS_FILE_BASE_PATH\", \"/home/flipt/secrets\")\n\n// Vault secrets\nflipt = flipt.\n    WithEnvVariable(\"FLIPT_SECRETS_PROVIDERS_VAULT_ENABLED\", \"true\").\n    WithEnvVariable(\"FLIPT_SECRETS_PROVIDERS_VAULT_ADDRESS\", \"http://vault:8200\")\n```\n\n## Coverage Collection\n\n### Go Coverage\n\n- Unit tests: Standard Go coverage with `go test -coverprofile`\n- Integration tests: Uses `GOCOVERDIR` environment variable for runtime coverage\n- Combined reporting via Codecov\n\n### UI Coverage\n\n- Jest for unit tests\n- Playwright for E2E tests\n- Coverage reports integrated with Codecov\n\n## Development Workflow\n\n### Pre-commit Checks\n\nAlways run before  # Lint UI code\n```\n\n### Adding New Integration Tests\n\n1. **Add test case** to `AllCases` map in `build/testing/integration.go`\n2. **Create test function** following existing patterns\n3. **Add Resource Management\n\n- Tests timeout after 20 minutes\n- Matrix execution distributes load across GitHub runners\n- Coverage aggregation minimizes storage overhead\n\n## Troubleshooting\n\n### This implementation provides:\n\n1. **Dynamic credential refresh** - Automatically obtains fresh ECR authorization tokens on each request\n2. **AWS credential chain support** - Leverages AWS SDK's credential chain for maximum flexibility\n3. **Temporary token handling** - Properly handles ECR's 12-hour temporary tokens\n4. **Backward compatibility** - Existing static credential authentication continues to work\n\n## Configuration\n\n### Basic Usage with AWS Chain\n\nTo configure Flipt to use AWS ECR authentication via the credential chain:\n\n```yaml\ncredentials:\n  ecr:\n    type: aws_chain\n    aws_chain:\n      region: us-east-1\n```\n\n### Configuration Options\n\nThe `aws_chain` credential type supports:\n\n- **region** (optional): AWS region for ECR service. If not specified, AWS SDK will use environment variables or instance metadata.\n\n### AWS Credential Chain\n\nThe AWS credential chain automatically checks credentials in the following order:\n\n1. Environment variables (`AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID`, `AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY`, `AWS_SESSION_TOKEN`)\n2. IAM roles (EC2, ECS, Lambda)\n3. ECS task credentials\n4. Web identity (OIDC)\n5. SSO profiles\n6. Shared credentials file (`~/.aws/credentials`)\n7. Shared config file (`~/.aws/config`)\n\n## Implementation Details\n\n### Components\n\n#### 1. Configuration (`internal/config/credentials.go`)\n\n- **`CredentialTypeAWSChain`**: New credential type constant\n- **`AWSChainConfig`**: Configuration structure with optional region field\n- Validation for AWS chain configuration\n\n#### 2. Credentials Provider (`internal/credentials/credentials.go`)\n\n- **`AWSECRAuth`**: Implements `githttp.AuthMethod` interface for ECR authentication\n- **`getECRAuthToken()`**: Retrieves temporary authorization tokens from AWS ECR\n- **`SetAuth()`**: Sets authorization headers on HTTP requests with fresh tokens\n\n#### 3. Testing (`internal/credentials/credentials_test.go`, `internal/config/credentials_test.go`)\n\n- Tests for AWS chain credential validation\n- Tests for credential retrieval and authentication\n- Tests for configuration options\n\n### How It Works\n\n1. **Configuration**: User specifies `type: aws_chain` in credentials config\n2. **Initialization**: When credentials are requested, AWS SDK initializes the credential chain\n3. **Token Retrieval**: On each git operation that requires authentication:\n   - The `SetAuth()` method calls `getECRAuthToken()`\n   - `getECRAuthToken()` calls AWS ECR's `GetAuthorizationToken` API\n   - The API returns a temporary token valid for 12 hours\n   - The token is base64-decoded and used as HTTP Basic Auth credentials\n4. **Automatic Refresh**: Since tokens are fetched on each request, expiration is automatically handled\n\n## Usage Examples\n\n### Example 1: Using IAM Role (EC2/ECS/Lambda)\n\nWhen running on AWS infrastructure with an IAM role attached:\n\n```yaml\nstorage:\n  default:\n    remote: 123456789012.dkr.ecr.us-east-1.amazonaws.com/my-bundle\n    branch: main\n\ncredentials:\n  ecr:\n    type: aws_chain\n    aws_chain:\n      region: us-east-1\n```\n\nThe credential chain will automatically use the instance IAM role.\n\n### Example 2: Using Environment Variables\n\n```bash\nexport AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID=AKIAIOSFODNN7EXAMPLE\nexport AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY=wJalrXUtnFEMI/K7MDENG/bPxRfiCYEXAMPLEKEY\nexport AWS_REGION=us-east-1\n\nflipt server --config config.yml\n```\n\n### Example 3: Using SSO Profile\n\n```bash\naws sso login --profile my-profile\n\nflipt server --config config.yml\n```\n\nWith configuration:\n\n```yaml\ncredentials:\n  ecr:\n    type: aws_chain\n    aws_chain:\n      region: us-east-1\n```\n\n## Security Considerations\n\n1. **Temporary Tokens**: ECR tokens are temporary (valid for 12 hours) and automatically refreshed\n2. **No Token Caching**: Tokens are fetched fresh on each request to ensure validity\n3. **Secure Credential Chain**: Credentials are handled securely by AWS SDK\n4. **IAM Policies**: Ensure IAM users/roles have `ecr:GetAuthorizationToken` permission\n\n### Required IAM Permissions\n\n```json\n{\n  \"Version\": \"2012-10-17\",\n  \"Statement\": [\n    {\n      \"Effect\": \"Allow\",\n      \"Action\": [\n        \"ecr:GetAuthorizationToken\"\n      ],\n      \"Resource\": \"*\"\n    },\n    {\n      \"Effect\": \"Allow\",\n      \"Action\": [\n        \"ecr:DescribeImages\",\n        \"ecr:DescribeRepositories\",\n        \"ecr:GetDownloadUrlForLayer\",\n        \"ecr:BatchGetImage\",\n        \"ecr:BatchGetRepositoryScanningConfiguration\"\n      ],\n      \"Resource\": \"arn:aws:ecr:*:123456789012:repository/my-bundle\"\n    }\n  ]\n}\n```\n\n## Backward Compatibility\n\nThis implementation maintains full backward compatibility with existing authentication methods:\n\n- **Basic Auth**: `type: basic` - continues to work as before\n- **SSH**: `type: ssh` - continues to work as before\n- **Access Tokens**: `type: access_token` - continues to work as before\n- **GitHub App**: `type: github_app` - continues to work as before\n\n## Testing\n\n### Unit Tests\n\nRun the credentials tests:\n\n```bash\ngo test ./internal/credentials -v\ngo test ./internal/config -v\n```\n\n### Integration Testing\n\nTo test with actual AWS ECR:\n\n1. Ensure you have AWS credentials configured\n2. Create an ECR repository\n3. Configure Flipt with the ECR repository URL\n4. Monitor logs for successful authentication:\n\n```\nlevel=info msg=\"pulling from remote\" environment=default remote=123456789012.dkr.ecr.us-east-1.amazonaws.com/my-bundle\n```\n\n## Troubleshooting\n\n### \"no AWS credentials available in credential chain\"\n\n**Cause**: No valid AWS credentials found in the credential chain.\n\n**Solution**:\n1. Verify AWS credentials are configured via environment variables, IAM role, or config file\n2. Ensure the IAM role/user has `ecr:GetAuthorizationToken` permission\n3. Check AWS configuration with: `aws sts get-caller-identity`\n\n### \"failed to get ECR authorization token\"\n\n**Cause**: AWS API call failed.\n\n**Solution**:\n1. Verify ECR repository exists and is in the correct region\n2. Check IAM permissions for the principal\n3. Verify network connectivity to AWS API endpoints\n\n### \"invalid ECR authorization token format\"\n\n**Cause**: ECR returned an invalid token format.\n\n**Solution**:\n1. This is rare - check AWS service status\n2. Verify using AWS CLI: `aws ecr get-authorization-token --region us-east-1`\n\n## Future Enhancements\n\n1. **Token Caching**: Implement optional token caching with expiration tracking\n2. **Multiple Registries**: Support different credentials for different ECR registries\n3. **Assume Role**: Support AWS STS AssumeRole for cross-account access\n4. **Custom Endpoints**: Support private ECR endpoints\n\n## References\n\n- [AWS SDK for Go v2](https://github.com/aws/aws-sdk-go-v2)\n- [AWS ECR GetAuthorizationToken API](https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonECR/latest/APIReference/API_GetAuthorizationToken.html)\n- [AWS Credential Providers](https://docs.aws.amazon.com/sdk-for-go/v1/developer-guide/configuring-sdk.html)\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":0,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1104,"cache_read_input_tokens":99130,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1104},"output_tokens":4,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"a2c9073b-8b0c-4050-b8db-5889f5358aae","uuid":"77c042c7-7eba-49b1-8a2d-52b83a01545f"}

This implementation provides:\n\n1. **Dynamic credential refresh** - Automatically obtains fresh ECR authorization tokens on each request\n2. **AWS credential chain support** - Leverages AWS SDK's credential chain for maximum flexibility\n3. **Temporary token handling** - Properly handles ECR's 12-hour temporary tokens\n4. **Backward compatibility** - Existing static credential authentication continues to work\n\n## Configuration\n\n### Basic Usage with AWS Chain\n\nTo configure Flipt to use AWS ECR authentication via the credential chain:\n\n```yaml\ncredentials:\n  ecr:\n    type: aws_chain\n    aws_chain:\n      region: us-east-1\n```\n\n### Configuration Options\n\nThe `aws_chain` credential type supports:\n\n- **region** (optional): AWS region for ECR service. Environment variables (`AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID`, `AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY`, `AWS_SESSION_TOKEN`)\n2. IAM roles (EC2, ECS, Lambda)\n3. ECS task credentials\n4. Web identity (OIDC)\n5. SSO profiles\n6. Shared credentials file (`~/.aws/credentials`)\n7. Shared config file (`~/.aws/config`)\n\n## Implementation Details\n\n### Components\n\n#### 1. Configuration (`internal/config/credentials.go`)\n\n- **`CredentialTypeAWSChain`**: New credential type constant\n- **`AWSChainConfig`**: Configuration structure with optional region field\n- Validation for AWS chain configuration\n\n#### 2. Credentials Provider (`internal/credentials/credentials.go`)\n\n- **`AWSECRAuth`**: Implements `githttp.AuthMethod` interface for ECR authentication\n- **`getECRAuthToken()`**: Retrieves temporary authorization tokens from AWS ECR\n- **`SetAuth()`**: Sets authorization headers on HTTP requests with fresh tokens\n\n#### 3. Testing (`internal/credentials/credentials_test.go`, `internal/config/credentials_test.go`)\n\n- Tests for AWS chain credential validation\n- Tests for credential retrieval and authentication\n- Tests for configuration options\n\n### How It Works\n\n1. **Configuration**: User specifies `type: aws_chain` in credentials config\n2. **Initialization**: When credentials are requested, AWS SDK initializes the credential chain\n3. **Token Retrieval**: On each git operation that requires authentication:\n   - The `SetAuth()` method calls `getECRAuthToken()`\n   - `getECRAuthToken()` calls AWS ECR's `GetAuthorizationToken` API\n   - The API returns a temporary token valid for 12 hours\n   - The token is base64-decoded and used as HTTP Basic Auth credentials\n4. **Automatic Refresh**: Since tokens are fetched on each request, expiration is automatically handled\n\n## Usage Examples\n\n### Example 1: Using IAM Role (EC2/ECS/Lambda)\n\nWhen running on AWS infrastructure with an IAM role      region: us-east-1\n```\n\n## Security Considerations\n\n1. **Temporary Tokens**: ECR tokens are temporary (valid for 12 hours) and automatically refreshed\n2. **No Token Caching**: Tokens are fetched fresh on each request to ensure validity\n3. **Secure Credential Chain**: Credentials are handled securely by AWS SDK\n4. **IAM Policies**: Ensure IAM users/roles have `ecr:GetAuthorizationToken` permission\n\n### Required IAM Permissions\n\n```json\n{\n  \"Version\": \"2012-10-17\",\n  \"Statement\": [\n    {\n      \"Effect\": \"Allow\",\n      \"Action\": [\n \"ecr:DescribeRepositories\",\n        \"ecr:GetDownloadUrlForLayer\",\n        \"ecr:BatchGetImage\",\n        \"ecr:BatchGetRepositoryScanningConfiguration\"\n      ],\n      \"Resource\": \"arn:aws:ecr:*:123456789012:repository/my-bundle\"\n    }\n  ]\n}\n```\n\n## Backward Compatibility\n\nThis implementation maintains full backward compatibility with existing authentication methods:\n\n- **Basic Auth**: `type: basic` - continues to work as before\n- **SSH**: `type: ssh` - continues to work as before\n- **Access Tokens**: `type: access_token` - continues to work as before\n- **GitHub App**: `type: github_app` - continues to work as before\n\n## Testing\n\n### Unit Tests\n\nRun the credentials tests:\n\n```bash\ngo test ./internal/credentials -v\ngo test ./internal/config -v\n```\n\n### Integration Testing\n\nTo test with actual AWS ECR:\n\n1. Ensure you have AWS credentials configured\n2. Create an ECR repository\n3. Configure Flipt with the ECR repository URL\n4. Monitor logs for successful authentication:\n\n```\nlevel=info msg=\"pulling from remote\" environment=default remote=123456789012.dkr.ecr.us-east-1.amazonaws.com/my-bundle\n```\n\n## Troubleshooting\n\n### \"no AWS credentials available in credential chain\"\n\n**Cause**: No valid AWS credentials found in the credential chain.\n\n**Solution**:\n1. Verify AWS credentials are configured via environment variables, IAM role, or config file\n2. Ensure the IAM role/user has `ecr:GetAuthorizationToken` permission\n3. Check AWS configuration with: `aws sts get-caller-identity`\n\n### \"failed to get ECR authorization token\"\n\n**Cause**: AWS API call failed.\n\n**Solution**:\n1. Verify ECR repository exists and is in the correct region\n2. Check IAM permissions for the principal\n3. Verify network connectivity to AWS API endpoints\n\n### \"invalid ECR authorization token format\"\n\n**Cause**: ECR returned an invalid token format.\n\n**Solution**:\n1. This is rare - check AWS service status\n2. Verify using AWS CLI: `aws ecr get-authorization-token --region us-east-1`\n\n## Future Enhancements\n\n1. **Token Caching**: Implement optional token caching with expiration tracking\n2. **Multiple Registries**: Support different credentials for different ECR registries\n3. **Assume Role**: Support AWS STS AssumeRole for cross-account access\n4. **Custom Endpoints**: Support private ECR endpoints\n\n## References\n\n- [AWS SDK for Go v2](https://github.com/aws/aws-sdk-go-v2)\n- [AWS ECR GetAuthorizationToken API](https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonECR/latest/APIReference/API_GetAuthorizationToken.html)\n- [AWS Credential Providers](https://docs.aws.amazon.com/sdk-for-go/v1/developer-guide/configuring-sdk.html)\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
